<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_15269971">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15269971" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/542037-annalisa" class="left imgcol" title="Annalisa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1226336540p2/542037.jpg" alt="Annalisa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/15269971?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 15, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/542037-annalisa" class="user" title="Annalisa">Annalisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=audiobook" class="actionLinkLite">audiobook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=literary" class="actionLinkLite">literary</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15269971">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6780199575798415">I get the point of the novel: to give a glimpse of small town life without extravagance. Beauty in simplicity. But I felt more depressed then touched by Haruf's picture of a whole town of people lonely in their own selfish wandering aimlessly without direction. I didn't like any characters in the book, except for maybe the boys who weren't old enough to yet become bitter, mean, and immoral. Nobody else in the book cared about anyone else as they focused on their small lives. Nobody did anything</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6780199575798415">I get the point of the novel: to give a glimpse of small town life without extravagance. Beauty in simplicity. But I felt more depressed then touched by Haruf's picture of a whole town of people lonely in their own selfish wandering aimlessly without direction. I didn't like any characters in the book, except for maybe the boys who weren't old enough to yet become bitter, mean, and immoral. Nobody else in the book cared about anyone else as they focused on their small lives. Nobody did anything for another person unless thrust upon them. Every last one of them was swallowed up by an environment that dampened motivation, optimism, love until the whole town was just going through the motions worried only about how daily life and others were affecting them. Nobody made me care what became of them and I did not relate to a single one of them. I understand that just plain people is the point, but I suppose my issue is that I disagree with Haruf's interpretation of life. All people have redeeming qualities and I have found that most people are likable. These people were not. It saddened me that someone would think that empty souls is what ordinary life is all about. I wanted to feel something for anyone, anything in the book, but I did not. I didn't learn anything nor was I left with any lingering sensation or thought and it wasn't the type of book that was just an enjoyable read and I could get caught up in the story. I suppose that's the thing with art is that a piece of work that will touch one person is just a collection of strokes to another and this was not a piece of art that grabbed by attention.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6780199575798415">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17933493826686699889">I think you missed the point this story is about the healing power of love. The story lays out the bleak everyday lives of this small town group. The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17933493826686699889">I think you missed the point this story is about the healing power of love. The story lays out the bleak everyday lives of this small town group. The pregnant 17 year old is thrown out by her mother. Her teacher helps her find a home with two elderly, unmarried farming brothers. They take her in and protect her and her baby despite the fact that they barely communicate with the outside world. In fact, i'd call then recluses. Here is the beauty of the story. Their generosity allows them to make a place for her. They are even a little afraid of her, but they respect her. They grow to love her and she them. That love heals them all.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/17606775?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 12, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/959013-rachel-bash" class="user" title="Rachel Bash">Rachel Bash</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17606775">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5201350873703375448">I'm from the Midwest, and though I agree with my East and West coast friends about some of its annoying (even madening) attributes (odd worship of football for one), I still believe it has a quiet, plain, yet surprising beauty all its own. This book captures that perfectly--the prose is spare, wiped clean of word-clutter, like the view I get out my window as I drive home across Iowa's corn fields. It's unadorned, but beautiful and communicative for that; because it says so little, what it does s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5201350873703375448">I'm from the Midwest, and though I agree with my East and West coast friends about some of its annoying (even madening) attributes (odd worship of football for one), I still believe it has a quiet, plain, yet surprising beauty all its own. This book captures that perfectly--the prose is spare, wiped clean of word-clutter, like the view I get out my window as I drive home across Iowa's corn fields. It's unadorned, but beautiful and communicative for that; because it says so little, what it does say stuns, amuses, punches in the gut. Kurt Vonnegut once said that the most powerful sentence in James Joyce's "Eveline" came towards the end, as she faced the inevitable: "She was tired." That's the kind of resonance I find here. Characters come to life on the sparest of stages, and perhaps because they stand out so strong against that stark background, it's easy to love them. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5201350873703375448">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1371542507?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 25, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1736960-kalen" class="user" title="Kalen">Kalen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1736960-kalen?shelf=2015-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2015-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1371542507">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2546295572222686006">I don't even know where to start with this book and I'm sure I'll be coming back to this over the next few days to edit and add things I forgot. <br /><br />Why did it take me so long to read Kent Haruf? I think a lot of it is that I worried he was too "blokey" for me and I wouldn't connect with the story or the characters. I sure was wrong. <br /><br />Haruf's writing is beautiful and bare, like the landscape in which Plainsong is set. You can feel the winter wind and see the dust. His characters and his book are quie</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2546295572222686006">I don't even know where to start with this book and I'm sure I'll be coming back to this over the next few days to edit and add things I forgot. <br /><br />Why did it take me so long to read Kent Haruf? I think a lot of it is that I worried he was too "blokey" for me and I wouldn't connect with the story or the characters. I sure was wrong. <br /><br />Haruf's writing is beautiful and bare, like the landscape in which Plainsong is set. You can feel the winter wind and see the dust. His characters and his book are quiet but solid. <br /><br />This book isn't perfect. Sometimes the dialogue is stilted. There are farm happenings that are unpleasant to read. But still this book gets five starts because I was so wrapped up in it I didn't even want to come up for air. I loved Harold and Raymond, the McPheron brothers. Victoria made me so sad. All of the characters of the fictional Holt, Colorado will be with me for a long time. <br /><br />The only good thing about waiting this long to read Kent Haruf is that I have several more books left to read and I'll savor those. Sadly, there won't be anymore books since Haruf died last November. (Just months after I was honored to meet him at Mountains &amp; Plains.) He was a true treasure and everyone should read him. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2546295572222686006">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_154782159">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154782159" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1883816-barbara" class="left imgcol" title="Barbara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448379218p2/1883816.jpg" alt="Barbara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/154782159?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 12, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1883816-barbara" class="user" title="Barbara">Barbara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1412050.Plainsong" title="Hardcover 9780375406188" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Barbara by: </span>
      Debby Sisson
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer154782159">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13385399619354606746">This is a beautiful, tender rendering of a small, mid-western town called Holt and its surrounding communities. Haruf's narrative is simple, yet elegant; sweet, yet realistic, always totally compelling. I experienced many mood swings while reading, from tears to laughter and empathy to outrage.<br /><br />The characters continually evoke a strong sense of community throughout the novel. It was apparent that nothing remains secret in such an atmosphere, but the inhabitants often played their parts as a large</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13385399619354606746">This is a beautiful, tender rendering of a small, mid-western town called Holt and its surrounding communities. Haruf's narrative is simple, yet elegant; sweet, yet realistic, always totally compelling. I experienced many mood swings while reading, from tears to laughter and empathy to outrage.<br /><br />The characters continually evoke a strong sense of community throughout the novel. It was apparent that nothing remains secret in such an atmosphere, but the inhabitants often played their parts as a large family. Certainly Haruf demonstrated devastating cruelty among some, but he meaningfully captured the essence of decency in a community. One could visualize and share the emotions of the teen-age pregnant girl. Two little brothers, closely bound in their abandonment by their mother, were sweet and realistic. A lovely and sharp, wizened and debilitated, yet caring, elderly lady is there to offer her support. Most endearing of all, the two unpolished bachelor brothers rang true and with great clarity. They were magnificent in their uncomplicated ways!<br /><br />The flat, spare quality of the land and the countryside was vividly described. Hard working, simple folk worked in their farms or at their ranches which were far from luxurious atmospheres. As with all else in Haruf's novel, his gentle prose conveyed what life was there.<br /><br />It would be easy to continue to laud this creative offering, but I will conclude by stating that I look forward to reading more by this fine author. <br /><br />**************************************************************<br /><br /><u> SECOND READING (for Book Group)</u><br /><br />I cannot locate the means to enter this book twice. However, let it suffice to say that my assessment of this book remains unchanged. It is rare that I read books a second time, but I see an added value of detecting nuances that I had either forgotten or missed the first time. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13385399619354606746">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer922374183">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9051372862885919740">More of the same from Mr Haruf. He uses simple dialogue to develop entrancing tales about nobodies in small town/rural America. The locale doesn't matter: I have no doubt that people in rural areas the world over are dealing with the same challenges faced by Haruf's protagonists. He makes the mundane seem important while keeping the body count to a bare minimum.<br /><br />I didn't care for the fact that some threads of the story were left unresolved or left dangling. I know that some of these will be addre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9051372862885919740">More of the same from Mr Haruf. He uses simple dialogue to develop entrancing tales about nobodies in small town/rural America. The locale doesn't matter: I have no doubt that people in rural areas the world over are dealing with the same challenges faced by Haruf's protagonists. He makes the mundane seem important while keeping the body count to a bare minimum.<br /><br />I didn't care for the fact that some threads of the story were left unresolved or left dangling. I know that some of these will be addressed in another book, but I still found this ploy manipulative. I also felt that many of the characters weren't fully developed or their motives clearly established. Maybe I missed something. Still, I couldn't put the darned book down; he probably has me on the hook now.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9051372862885919740">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/374653-judy?shelf=bookgroup" class="actionLinkLite">bookgroup</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/374653-judy?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/374653-judy?shelf=novel" class="actionLinkLite">novel</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/374653-judy?shelf=good-for-book-group" class="actionLinkLite">good-for-book-group</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/374653-judy?shelf=small-town-character-driven" class="actionLinkLite">small-town-character-driven</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152201141">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15219361771704009981">I absolutely loved this book. I had downloaded a sample on my Kindle, and I liked it so much that I waited until I could get the book from a bookstore so that I could experience it fully. It follows the lives of some people in a small town in Colorado. It begins quietly, and continues with little ornamentation -- the title seems apt. It is subtle all the way through, but as in musical plainsong, the parts join together, making a greater whole. There is spare punctuation and no quotation marks, a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15219361771704009981">I absolutely loved this book. I had downloaded a sample on my Kindle, and I liked it so much that I waited until I could get the book from a bookstore so that I could experience it fully. It follows the lives of some people in a small town in Colorado. It begins quietly, and continues with little ornamentation -- the title seems apt. It is subtle all the way through, but as in musical plainsong, the parts join together, making a greater whole. There is spare punctuation and no quotation marks, allowing the words to build as if sliding downhill, gathering power as they go: <br /><br />"She shuffled into the next room and came back carrying a flat and ragged cardboard box and set it on the table and removed the lid, then she showed them photographs that had been much-handled in the long afternoons and evenings of her solitary life, photographs that had been lifted out and examined and returned to the black picture book album, the album itself of an old shape and style. They were all of her son, Albert. "<br /><br />The characters are dimensional, their flaws adding to their appeal.<br /><br />This would be a good read for book group.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15219361771704009981">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('48dIGykOhFDLVoeHhR17S/J9WhwimqdgbGEVKmirAOKGE3fI29yQqkeO8zz7fJ35u4qZBWtH4MoGaBC4pD72pw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16266.Kent_Haruf">About Kent Haruf</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/16266.Kent_Haruf"><img alt="16266" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1309205400p2/16266.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16414066918166469861">Kent Haruf was born in eastern Colorado. He received his Bachelors of Arts in literature from Nebraska Wesleyan University in 1965 and his Masters of Fine Arts from the Iowa Writers' Workshop at the University of Iowa in 1973. For two years, he taught English in Turkey with the Peace Corps and his other jobs have included a chicken farm in Colorado, a construction site in Wyoming, a rehabilitation</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16414066918166469861">Kent Haruf was born in eastern Colorado. He received his Bachelors of Arts in literature from Nebraska Wesleyan University in 1965 and his Masters of Fine Arts from the Iowa Writers' Workshop at the University of Iowa in 1973. For two years, he taught English in Turkey with the Peace Corps and his other jobs have included a chicken farm in Colorado, a construction site in Wyoming, a rehabilitation hospital in Colorado, a hospital in Arizona, a library in Iowa, an alternative high school in Wisconsin, and universities in Nebraska and Illinois.<br /><br />Haruf is the author of Plainsong, which received the Mountains and Plains Booksellers Award, the Los Angeles Times Book Prize, the Maria Thomas Award in Fiction, and The New Yorker Book Award. Plainsong was also a finalist for the 1999 National Book Award. His novel, The Tie That Binds, received a Whiting Foundation Award and a special citation from the Pen/Hemingway Foundation. In 2006, Haruf was awarded the Dos Passos Prize for Literature.<br /><br />All of his novels are set in the fictional town of Holt, Colorado. Holt is loosely based on Yuma, Colorado, an early residence of Haruf in the 1980s.<br /><br />Haruf lived with his wife, Cathy, in Salida, Colorado, with their three daughters. He died of cancer on November 30, 2014.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16414066918166469861">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/16266.Kent_Haruf" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Kent Haruf...</a>
